<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Simulation Study</h2></div><p>The aim of this section is to highlight and quantify the nonlinear contribution of the cooperative system above modeled. The power matching, multisource operation, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> rectification and its effects on the RF-to-dc conversion efficiency of the EEH-C are notably studied.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Contribution of the RFID Chip Nonlinearity</h3><p>In order to quantify the nonlinearity introduced by the RFID chip, i.e., the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> level, a linear model of the RFID chip is used as a comparative reference. The linear model, which does not produce any harmonic nor changes its impedance respect to the power, consists of the impedance file of the nonlinear RFID chip model calculated at its activation threshold.</p><p>Let assume an RFID reader that communicates with the augmented tag (considering 0 dB tag antenna gain) for 1 m distance between each other (i.e., 31.21 dB of propagation losses at 0.868 GHz). If the augmented tag sensitivity is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-9~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-9~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the power injected into node 1 of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, so-called <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, should be equal to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-9~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-9~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The maximum power injected into the same node, considering the propagation losses in agreement with the regulations <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4a">[28]</a> and so-called <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, would be approximately 5 dBm. Additionally, three WPT-S power configuration cases are defined:
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-6~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-6~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (case 1) which corresponds to the injected power into the augmented tag by a Wi-Fi router transmitting at its maximum allowed Equivalent Isotropic Radiated Power (EIRP), i.e., 36 dBm at 1 m distance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_4a">[21]</a>;</p></li><li><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-13~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-13~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (case 2) which corresponds to the injected power into the augmented tag by the same Wi-Fi router distanced 3 meters;</p></li><li><p>WPT-S is off (case 3).</p></li></ul><p></p><p>Hereinafter the values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the three WPT-S power configurations are kept constant for all the simulation tests.</p><p>In order to quantify <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in function of the reader power, the Power Spectral Density (PSD) calculated at the EEH-C input is analyzed at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm WPT}{-}{\rm S} = -6~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">{\rm WPT}{-}{\rm S} = -6~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 4</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">5</a> show the PSD for a linear chip model and for the chip producing harmonics, respectively. Thanks to the HB tool, the analysis of the linear chip allows determining the weak presence of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3^{\rm rd}</span><script type="math/tex">3^{\rm rd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> harmonic of the RFID reader signal produced by the EEH-C (indeed, the linear chip does not produce harmonics but the EEH-C is always nonlinear). The weak leakage of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-35~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-35~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is only distinguishable for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The analysis of the nonlinear chip model shows a greatly distinguishable <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> level: <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> reaches <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-27~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-27~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and more than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-10~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-10~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The rectification of this <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the aim of the intended multisource operation.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Power spectrum with linear RFID chip model. The PSD is taken at the input of the EEH section in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. There is not generation of harmonics due to the chip but a weak harmonic coming from the reader.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7327252/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Power spectrum with nonlinear RFID chip model. The PSD is taken at the input of the EEH section in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. The chip generates a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3^{\rm rd}</span><script type="math/tex">3^{\rm rd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> harmonic signal. The reader power slightly affects the signal level at 2.45 GHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7327252/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Finally, small variations on the 2.45 GHz signal strength due to the reader power injected into node 1 can be also observed. This phenomenon is studied in detail in subsequent paragraphs.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. System Performance</h3><p>The key parameter to evaluate the EEH-C performance is the RF-to-dc conversion efficiency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\eta)</span><script type="math/tex">(\eta)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> defined as the ratio of the dc output power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(P_{dc})</span><script type="math/tex">(P_{dc})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by the RF input power into the EEH-C <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(P_{RF})</span><script type="math/tex">(P_{RF})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Given the multisource operation and the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> exploitation approach, a fair evaluation of the EEH-C needs an accurate definition of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. From the PSD analysis shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>, the RF signals that significantly contribute to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{RF}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{RF}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are: the power at 0.868 GHz leaked from the reader <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(P_{RF@0.868})</span><script type="math/tex">(P_{RF@0.868})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the power at 2.45 GHz coming from the WPT-S <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(P_{RF@2.45})</span><script type="math/tex">(P_{RF@2.45})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and the power at 2.604 GHz due to the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> contribution <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(P_{RF@2.604})</span><script type="math/tex">(P_{RF@2.604})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The intermodulation products observed in the PSD are very weak and therefore noncontributory to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{RF}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{RF}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. With these considerations, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the EEH-C is defined in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a> <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta={{P_{dc}}\over{P_{RF}}}={{P_{dc}}\over{P_{RF@0.868}+P_{RF@2.45}+P_{RF@2.604}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(1)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\eta={{P_{dc}}\over{P_{RF}}}={{P_{dc}}\over{P_{RF@0.868}+P_{RF@2.45}+P_{RF@2.604}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(1)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eta={{P_{dc}}\over{P_{RF}}}={{P_{dc}}\over{P_{RF@0.868}+P_{RF@2.45}+P_{RF@2.604}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(1)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><div class="section_2" id="sec4b1"><h4>1. Effects of the Reader Power in the System</h4><p>In order to quantify the effect of the reader power and the contribution of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the EEH-C performance, <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> shows <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus the reader power injected into node 1 and for the different WPT-S configurations. Continuous lines represent <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with the chip model generating a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3^{\rm rd}</span><script type="math/tex">3^{\rm rd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> harmonic and dash lines represent <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with a linear chip model.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus the power received in node 1 from the reader. Continuous lines represent <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with the chip model generating a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3^{\rm rd}</span><script type="math/tex">3^{\rm rd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> harmonic and dash lines represent <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with a linear chip model. (a) and (b) Case 1, WPT-S equal to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-6~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-6~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (c) and (d) Case 2, WPT-S equal to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-13~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-13~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (e) and (f) Case 3, WPT-s off.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7327252/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The benefit, introduced only by the multisource operation, can be studied with the linear chip model when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is not present. Looking at <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> in curves (b) and (d) in where the multisource is set and a linear chip model is considered (i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> does not exist), the EEH-C conversion efficiency is higher respect to curve (f) in where only the reader is active.</p><p>The benefit introduced only by the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> rectification can be studied comparing the linear and nonlinear chip models when the WPT-S is off. Looking at <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> in curve (e) in where only the reader transmits and a nonlinear chip model is considered (i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> exists), the EEH-C conversion efficiency is higher respect to curve (f), in where the chip has a linear model. Indeed the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be increased, so also <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, by increasing the reader power. However at higher levels, due to the saturation behavior of the diode at large signals, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is limited and all curves converge.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b2"><h4>2. Effects of the WPT-S Power in the System</h4><p>Besides the contribution of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the effect of the WPT-S power in the EHH-C conversion performance is studied. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> shows <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus the WPT-S power for three power cases: <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and reader off, and for the two chip models (i.e., linear and nonlinear).
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus WPT-s power. Continuous lines represent <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with the chip model generating a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3^{\rm rd}</span><script type="math/tex">3^{\rm rd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> harmonic and dash lines represent <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with a linear chip model.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7327252/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>At low WPT-S power, the multisource operation cases (red and blue curves) allows achieving an enhancement of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> compared to the single WPT-S case (black curve), especially as high reader power. At high WPT-S power, the greater contributor to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the WPT-S, due to the optimized design of the EHH-C at 2.45 GHz. Combining both sources, in the best of the cases (blue curve with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in respect to black curve), an RF-to-dc conversion efficiency 55% greater than the case using only the WPT-S is achieved. As a result, the approach of improving <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by means of a multisource operation and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> rectification is demonstrated by simulations.</p></div></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Experimental Evaluation</h2></div><p>The aim of this section is to experimentally verify and quantify the nonlinear contribution of the proposed cooperative system considering a commercial RFID passive chip and also more complex WPT-S signals. As discussed in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>, alternatively a finite bandwidth signal with arbitrary modulation can be expressed mathematically in a general form as a (multi-harmonic) signal with a time-varying envelope. Based on the described concept an emulated prototype is designed, and two kinds of experiments are performed in order to evaluate the RF-to-dc conversion efficiency of the EEH section in function of: (i) the composite signal (<a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5a" class="fulltext-link">Section V-A</a>); (ii) the WPT-S waveform, i.e., a finite bandwidth signal with arbitrary modulation, (<a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5b" class="fulltext-link">Section V-B</a>).</p><p>The complete setup is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>. Specific details are below described.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>The RFID section is composed by two parts: (i) the antenna emulator composed by two impedance tuners Microlab SF-30F connected in series to offer a power matching between reader, chip and EHH section; (ii) the RFID chip EM4325 shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(a)</a> is fixed in a SMA connector <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_5">[9]</a>; when the matching is achieved, the chip response is detected by the reader.</p></li><li><p>The TPMN shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(b)</a> is emulated by the combination of the impedance tuners with a first <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">50~\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">50~\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> directional coupler with Coupling Factor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({\rm CF}= 25~{\rm dB})</span><script type="math/tex">({\rm CF}= 25~{\rm dB})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. A trade-off power matching is done by activating the chip while maximizing the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> level at the input of the EEH section.</p></li><li><p>A second directional coupler <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({\rm CF}=25~{\rm dB})</span><script type="math/tex">({\rm CF}=25~{\rm dB})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is used to couple the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with the WPT-S signal and feed the EEH section.</p></li><li><p>The EEH section shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(c)</a> is the same to the one designed in the simulation study. It is composed by a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">50~\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">50~\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> matching network in series with a single stage of a voltage doubler consisting of two Skyworks SMS7630 Schottkty diodes as in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_5">[13]</a>. The dc section at the output consists of a low-pass filter capacitor and a resistor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm R}_{\rm L~EEH}</span><script type="math/tex">{\rm R}_{\rm L~EEH}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in where the dc level is measured.</p></li><li><p>The Speedway Revolution RFID reader and an external source at 2.45 GHz (Agilent N5182A Vector Signal Generator (VSG)) represents the reader and the WPT-S respectively as above described.</p></li><li><p>For power tests, a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">50~\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">50~\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> digital Oscilloscope (Agilent 91204 DSO) is connected instead of the EEH section in order to measure the PSD of the input.</p></li></ul>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Measurement setup and emulated prototype. Schematic diagram at the top and implemented setup at the bottom. (a) RFID chip. (b) Three port matching network. (c) EEH section.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7327252/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Once all sections are integrated, a power matching trade-off is done with the impedance tuners. The principle is to activate the RFID chip (looking for the minimum chip activation threshold in the RFID reader) while maximizing the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> level at the input of the EEH section. The visualization of the PSD in the DSO allows performing this analysis.</p><p>Four main differences valorize this experimental evaluation from the reported one in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_5">[29]</a>: (i) the reader, that activates the RFID chip, is always present, and it varies its power; (ii) the losses in the system are reduced due to the use of two directional couplers instead of three; (iii) the dc output of the EHH-C is not connected to the dc input of the chip because of the intention to quantify its value; (iv) a new definition of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> presented in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4b" class="fulltext-link">Section IV-B</a>, allows evaluating the EEH-C more accurately.</p><p>Following the power limits defined in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4a" class="fulltext-link">Section IV-A</a>, and considering the described setup, the conducted power of the Speedway Revolution reader that activates the augmented tag is 17.5 dBm, and the maximum one is 31.5 dBm. After calibration, these values represent <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{1}= -9~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{1}= -9~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2} = 5~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2} = 5~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (subtracting 26.5 dB of losses in the coupled path of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> due to the CF and connectivity). Hereinafter the values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are kept constant for all experimental tests. These power settings allow calculating the scaled read range of the augmented tag. Always considering a tag antenna of 0 dB gain and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-9~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-9~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> sensitivity, a read range of 4.8 m is estimated in over-the-air configuration complying with the regulations <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_5">[28]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_5">[30]</a>. It is worth noting that the chip sensitivity of the chosen sample, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-9~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-9~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, is not affected by the system integration, therefore the standard reading range for tags using this kind of chip is respected.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec5a"><h3>A. Multisource Power Dependency</h3><p>This first analysis evaluates <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> under a multisource operation scenario, i.e., in terms of the power simultaneously emitted by the RFID reader and the WPT-S. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a> depicts the measured dc output versus the WPT-S power for the two reader power configurations and without reader. Results for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and reader off are quite close each other due to the losses introduced by the emulated TPMN; however the improvement of combining sources is still notable. Moreover, higher dc values are obtained for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Harvested dc output in function of the input power at 2.45 GHz. The experiment is performed for the two reader power configurations. Greater values are obtained when the reader transmits its maximum allowed, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7327252/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In order to accurately calculate <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a>, an experimental PSD analysis at the input of the EEH section is necessary. The analysis is possible thanks to the use of the DSO. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>, comparable with <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>, shows the normalized measured PSD of a multisource configuration (reader and WPT-S) firstly reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_5a">[29]</a>. When both sources are active, the PSD shows measurable values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{RF@0.868}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{RF@0.868}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (RFID communication signal), <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{RF@2.45}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{RF@2.45}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (signal to be harvested), and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{RF@2.604}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{RF@2.604}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to be harvested). Performing the analysis with the setup above described, the experimental calculation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is possible.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>Normalized power spectral density visualized on the DSO when the sections are interconnected in the setup reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_5a">[19]</a>. When both sources are active, a richest spectrum favors the conversion efficiency of the harvester circuit.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7327252/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a> shows <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus the WPT-S power for both reader configurations and without reader, and compares the results to the ones obtained by simulation at the lowest power. An improvement of 8% in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be noted for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at low WPT-S power (blue curve from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-30~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-30~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-20~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-20~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) compared to the single WPT-S operation (black curve). As a result, the behavior predicted by simulations in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4b" class="fulltext-link">Section IV-B</a> is verified by measurement, i.e., the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> combined with the WPT-S signal triggers in an enhanced <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Even if the magnitudes are less than the simulated ones (comparing simulated and measured cases); the experimental results validate the approach. Magnitude differences from the simulation results have two expected reasons: (i) losses in the emulated prototype (especially the use of a coupler in the TPMN and chip fixture); and (ii), differences in the commercial performance compared to the simulated model.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>RF-to-dc conversion efficiency of the EEH-c in function of the input power at 2.45 GHz. In dashed line the simulated values.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7327252/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5b"><h3>B. WPT-S Waveforms Dependency</h3><p>The previous tests have considered the WPT-S transmitting a CW tone. In this part, a time-varying envelope signal generated at the input of the EHH section by the composite signal composed by the tone triggered by the multisource operation of the system and the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3^{\rm rd}</span><script type="math/tex">3^{\rm rd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> harmonic RFID product. Hereinafter, and in addition to the composite tone signal approach, the WPT-S signal waveform is configured with the intention to study its effect on EEH section conversion efficiency. It is worth noting that during all tests the RFID reader and chip are communicating.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec5b1"><h4>1. Studied Waveforms and Their Characteristics</h4><p>At the input of the EHH section, four kinds of composite waveforms are studied by combining a modulated signal from the WPT-S with the leaked signal at 0.868 GHz and the redirected <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It is worth noting that the 0.868 GHz and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> signals are from the RFID communication using ASK modulation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_5b1">[28]</a>. In the WPT-S, three modulations commonly used in wireless systems are set, in addition to the CW tone: Orthogonal Frequency-Division Multiplexing (OFDM), Gaussian Minimum-Shift Keying (GMSK), and Amplitude-Shift Keying (ASK).</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a> shows the normalized PSD of the three modulated and the CW tone above considered. All signals are set with the same average power and centered at 2.45 GHz.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 12. </b><fig><p>Normalized power spectral density visualized on the DSO at the EEH input when the sections are interconnected. The average power is the same for all signals. 14 MHz are taking into account for the waveform analysis.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7327252/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Using a Tektronix RSA5000 Spectrum Analyzer in the position of the DSO in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>, the Complementary Cumulative Distribution Function (CCDF) of the envelope of the composite waveforms (WPT-S signal plus leaked 0.868 GHz signal and the redirected <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0chip}</span><script type="math/tex">3f_{0chip}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) in function of the distance to its average power in dB is measured and results are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13</a>. This plot gives information about the instantaneous power of the composite time signal. Actually, the value in where the CCDF curve intersects the x-axis indicates the maximum PAPR of the signal envelope; and therefore, the maximum PAPR of the signal can be estimated adding 3 dB to the PAPR of the signal envelope <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_5b1">[10]</a>. According to <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13</a>, composite signals using OFDM in the WPT-S have the highest PAPR, followed by the ones using ASK and finally, very close to each other, are the one using GMSK and the CW tone, with PAPR values very close to zero due to the almost null variation of the envelope.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig13"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-13-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-13-small.gif" alt="Figure 13" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 13. </b><fig><p>Measured CCDF of the envelope of the test signals.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7327252/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5b2"><h4>2. Effect of the Waveform in the Conversion Efficiency</h4><p>In order to evaluate <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> when different waveforms are used to operate the EEH section, the signal power is evaluated as the total average power in 14 MHz bandwidth around the carrier (see in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a>). An accurate evaluation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> should also consider the effect of the reader (the signal level entering to the EEH section at 2.45 GHz is slightly affected by the reader power as seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>), in this context a figure of gain is defined in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a> <disp-formula id="deqn2" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox {Efficiency gain}}=10\log\left({{\eta_{power_{2}}}\over{\eta_{power_{1}}}}\right)\eqno{\hbox{(2)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">{\hbox {Efficiency gain}}=10\log\left({{\eta_{power_{2}}}\over{\eta_{power_{1}}}}\right)\eqno{\hbox{(2)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\hbox {Efficiency gain}}=10\log\left({{\eta_{power_{2}}}\over{\eta_{power_{1}}}}\right)\eqno{\hbox{(2)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{Power_{1}}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{Power_{1}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{Power_{2}}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{Power_{2}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are the conversion efficiency of the EEH-C calculated for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively.</p><p>Measured values of the conversion efficiency and the power harvested in the EEH-C load are unfolded in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a> for the limit power configuration cases, and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a> depicts the figure of gain for each kind of waveforms.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig14"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-14-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-fig-14-small.gif" alt="Figure 14" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 14. </b><fig><p>Figure of gain in the conversion efficiency defined as in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7327252/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table II </b>Conversion efficiency and harvested power in the EEH-c load for different waveforms<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7343796/7327252/7327252-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>At low WPT-S (“a” columns in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>), higher gain is obtained combining an optimum waveform with a high reader signal power, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. At high WPT-S power, i.e., above <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-13~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-13~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a>. (“b” column in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>), a negative figure of gain is obtained. This means that in a relative comparison, a higher <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta</span><script type="math/tex">\eta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is obtained when the WPT-S signals are combined with low power from the reader, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Power_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">Power_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as depicted in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>. The same effect is explained in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4b2" class="fulltext-link">Section IV-B2</a> (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>) for the case of CW tone.</p><p>Reported results show that the waveform can enhance the RF-to-dc conversion efficiency of the EEH-C. Considering the CCDF analysis, OFDM and ASK signals produce higher conversion efficiency because of their higher PAPR compared to GSM and CW signals <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_5b2">[10]</a>. The findings of using waveforms with high PAPR in order to increase the conversion efficiency agree with results postulated in the literature <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_5b2">[10]</a>,<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_5b2">[12]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_5b2">[14]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_5b2">[15]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_5b2">[16]</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_5b2">[17]</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_5b2">[18]</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_5b2">[19]</a>.</p></div></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>Conclusion and Discussion</h2></div><p>Nowadays RFID is a well-established technology for identification purposes. Moreover, due to its huge practical advantages such as passive and wireless features, it is more and more considered in order to enable many other applications under the paradigm of Internet of Things. This mainly consists to integrate more of functionalities to the RFID tags such as sensing and localization capabilities. Such an evolution of RFID tag structures requires new additional source of energy and also its optimized management.</p><p>This paper proposes and demonstrates the cooperative exploitation of two effects in order to improve the power budget available for augmented passive RFID tags. The first effect is related to the non-linearity of RFID chip that generates wasted power at the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3^{\rm rd}</span><script type="math/tex">3^{\rm rd}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> harmonic of fundamental frequency, i.e., 868 MHz in Europe. The second effect lies in the enhancing of the RF-dc conversion efficiency of rectifier circuits by applying multi-frequency excitation signal. Combining the exploitation of these two effects, a unique design is simulated and experimentally emulated. The developed prototype consists of an emulated RFID tag operating at 868 MHz and an Electromagnetic Energy Harvesting circuit operating at the 2.45 GHz ISM band corresponding to existing ambient transmissions, both integrated to operate with a mutual enhanced performance. Moreover, since the composite energy harvesting system exploits the nonlinear i-v characteristic of rectifier circuits using time-varying envelope signals, experiments using different waveforms, i.e., different digitally modulated signals in the 2.45 GHz source are performed. It is worth noting that the emulated prototype has not as objective to reproduce the simulated performances but to validate the exposed concepts using a commercial RFID chip. Three significant results are highlighted:
</p><ol><li><p>Simulation results based on a simplified chip model show enhancement in the RF-to-dc conversion efficiency when the cooperative operation, considering the RFID chip non-linearity is established. The conversion efficiency rises from 1% when the 2.45 GHz source transmits at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-30~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-30~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the RFID reader is off to 56% when the power injected into the augmented tag at 2.45 GHz (external source) is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-30~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-30~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the power injected at 0.868 GHz (RFID reader) is 5 dBm.</p></li><li><p>Experimental results also demonstrate an improvement in the RF-to-dc conversion efficiency when the cooperative operation, considering a commercial RFID chip and an emulated prototype, is established. An 8% enhancement in the conversion efficiency is achieved when the power injected into the tag at 2.45 GHz (using a CW tone) is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-30~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-30~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the power injected at 0.868 GHz is 5 dBm.</p></li><li><p>Experimental results show an RF-to-dc conversion efficiency enhancement using composite signals with high PAPR. The conversion efficiency rises from 14.41% when the composite system uses a CW signal at 2.45 GHz to 23.16% when it uses an OFDM signal. In this case the power injected into the tag at 2.45 GHz is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-6~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-6~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the power injected at 0.868 GHz is equal to the tag sensitivity i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-9~{\rm dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-9~{\rm dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and represents 4.8 m of estimated tag read range.</p></li></ol><p></p><p>Finally in terms of perspectives, further efforts can be devoted to the use of the cooperative integration milestones exposed in this paper in order to design a single and miniaturized device. Regarding the tag size, a final prototype of the augmented tag may be comparable with current passive RFID tags, e.g., a credit card size using a double face structure integrating an antenna and reducing costs seems feasible <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_6">[24]</a>.</p><p>Otherwise, the additional power produced by the cooperative RF harvesting could be profited by low-consumption electronics, e.g., humidity, temperature <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_6">[24]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref25" id="context_ref_25_6">[25]</a>, or air pollution sensors like the CleanSpace-Tag from Drayson-Technologies. Such an enhancement can be also potentially empowered in indoor scenarios where Wi-Fi sources can be seen as hot spots of the application. Furthermore, the read range enhancement can be an option when considerable power is harvested from the additional source (e.g., 2.45 GHz) compensating the propagation losses at 868 MHz.</p></div>
</div></div>

He became University Full Professor in 1993 and since 1996 he is Professor at the esisar, Embedded Systems Department of Grenoble-inp. His main teaching topics concern applied electromagnetism, radio frequency, wireless systems and optoelectronics. He has more than 30 years experience in academic education, research and management of university affairs. He served as coordinator and staff member in numerous academic programs both for education and research. He was coordinator for Ph.D. program, Master's and Bachelor's Programs for the Universities at Grenoble, some of these programs are under collaboration with international universities from Europe, Canada, Brazil, Vietnam, Egypt, and Maghreb. He served as the Director of esisar, Grenoble-inp. His main topics in research are applied electromagnetism, modeling of devices and circuits at both RF and optoelectronic domains. His current research concerns wireless systems with specific attention to RFID technology and its applications. He is the Founder and past Director of the LCIS Lab. He is the founder of ORSYS group and he leaded this group 2008–2014. He supervised more than 35 PhD and he has more than 250 publications. He serves as Examiner-reviewer for tens of Ph.D. degrees for universities in many countries (France, Germany, Finland, Spain, Ireland, Italy, Sweden, Vietnam, Australia, Singapore, India, Brazil, Egypt, Maghreb).</div><!-- end ngRepeat: biop in ::item.bio.p --><div class="pure-u-24-24 u-mt-1 ng-binding ng-scope" ng-repeat="biop in ::item.bio.p">Dr. Tedjini is a ember of several TPC and serves as expert reviewer for national and international scientific committees and conferences including journals such Piers, IEEE (MTT, AP, Sensors, MWCL), URSI, ISO, ANR, OSEO, FNQRT. He organized several conferences-workshops and was TPC chair-co-chair in numerous conferences. Recently he was the General Chair of IEEE RFID-TA 2012. Senior Member IEEE, President and founder of the EEE-CPMT French Chapter, Vice-President of IEEE Section France and elected as the Vice-Chair of URSI Commission D Electronics and Photonics in 2008. He was reelected as vice-chair of IEEE-France-section and he is serving as the Chair of URSI Commission D for the triennium 2011–2014. In particular the preparation on the General Assembly and Scientific Symposium which was held in Beijing August 2014. Recently he was elected as the President of URSI-France 2015–2018. Now, Smail Tedjini is leading several research contracts. He is supervising several Ph.D. students and post-doc. <script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

The objective is to exploit the i-v nonlinearity of the rectifier by applying a signal with time-varying envelope in order to improve the RF-to-dc conversion efficiency. Thanks to a multisource configuration, i.e., an RFID reader at 0.868 GHz and an external source at 2.45 GHz, the EEH-C is able to rectify the 3&lt;sup&gt;rd&lt;/sup&gt; harmonic product of the RFID chip, in addition to the 2.45 GHz signal, without compromising the RFID communication. Additionally, digitally modulated signals are used at 2.45 GHz to further enhance the harvesting efficiency of the EEH-C.
